Saving Snack Money to Help the Righteous Army

Zheng Xingxian (12 years old) and Zheng Fengxian (9 years old), two sisters who are female students at the private Shihua Primary School on Beikaier Road in Eastern Shanghai, heard the principal, Xu Songting, report on the situation of the Northeast War during the school's memorial week last Monday. He mentioned that barbaric and inhumane troops were constantly attacking our isolated and helpless righteous army, who were fighting in the freezing cold and starving, etc. Therefore, the two primary school students voluntarily donated 14 yuan, which they had saved from their usual snack money, and purchased donation books to solicit donations from their relatives and classmates. As of yesterday, they had raised 244 yuan. The Municipal Government Orders the Social Affairs Bureau to Resolve the Outstanding Case of the Yong'an No. 2 Factory

Party and Government Agencies Have Begun Mediation

But Both Sides Insist, and the Situation Deteriorates

All the workers of the Yong'an Textile No. 2 Factory in Wusong demanded the distribution of bonuses, and on December 20th of the year before last, a tragedy occurred. A female worker, Jiao Lianying, was strangled to death, and twelve people, including Shen Yongming, were arrested. During the trial in the court, three of the deceased died. Later, the Jiangsu High Court acquitted and released them. However, the case remained unresolved. Recently, the Municipal Government ordered the Social Affairs Bureau to find a way to resolve the outstanding case. The details are as follows:

Municipal Government Order: The Eighth District Cotton Textile Industry Union has petitioned the Party and Government agencies, requesting them to promptly resolve the outstanding cases, including: 1. Four months' bonus for the 20th year; 2. Wage during the statutory revolutionary memorial day off for the 20th year; 3. Reinstatement of workers who were dismissed without reason and workers who were illegally dismissed by the local court prosecutor; 4. Strict order to the factory to fulfill the labor-management agreement which was violated by the employer; 5. The employer should be ordered to provide compensation to the dead and injured workers. After the Eighth District Party Headquarters submitted the request, the Municipal Government instructed the Social Affairs Bureau to investigate and respond accordingly.

Party and Government Mediation: Yesterday, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau sent Wang Gang, a staff member of the Third Section, and the Municipal Party Headquarters sent Lu Yinchu, a staff member of the People's Training Section, to jointly mediate. They also summoned the Yong'an No. 2 Factory of the Eighth District Cotton Textile Union for questioning. Representatives from the employer, Chen Caisheng and He Boxuan, and representatives from the labor side, Wang Yuncheng and Jin Yaowen, arrived. The labor side demanded the execution and resolution of the outstanding cases. The employer believed that there had never been a bonus in the past, that it was impossible to reinstate the dismissed workers, and that there was no precedent for wages on memorial days, making mediation impossible. Currently, the Party and Government agencies are carefully considering concrete solutions.

The Post Office Modified Insurance Rates for Insured Mail to Japan and Other Places Starting Yesterday

The Shanghai Postal Administration announced: "Starting February 1st of this year, the maximum insurance amount and fees for insured parcels, insured letters, and insured letter boxes sent to Japan, Korea, Kwantung, leased territories, and Taiwan will be modified as follows: 1. Insured letters: In addition to the regular postage and registration fee, an insurance fee of one dime will be charged for every 120 yuan insured, or any fraction thereof; 2. Insured letter boxes: In addition to the regular postage of eight cents per 50 centimeters of weight (postage starts at 40 cents), an insurance fee of one dime will be charged for each amount added. For both of the above items, the maximum amount of insurance is set at 1,000 yuan; 3. Parcel insurance fee: A fee of 20 cents will be charged for the insured amount not exceeding 120 silver dollars. An additional 10 cents will be charged for each additional 120 silver dollars insured, or any fraction thereof. The maximum insured amount for post offices marked with the word "货(一)" [Cargo 1] in the list of postal locations can reach 1,000 yuan, and for post offices marked with the word "货" [Cargo], it is limited to 500 yuan."

The Bureau of Finance Began Collecting Entertainment Tax Yesterday

Dedicated to Relieving Northeast Refugees

Guomin News Agency reported that in view of the displacement of Northeast refugees, the central government proposed to the Executive Yuan that a relief donation for Northeast refugees should be levied on entertainment venues across the country. The Municipal Bureau of Finance also started yesterday (the 1st). The regulations set by the bureau are copied below: "Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Finance's Measures for Levying Relief Donations for Northeast Refugees at Entertainment Venues." 1. All movie theaters, theaters, and entertainment venues should strictly comply with the central government's order to collect a relief donation of 10% on the price of their tickets or seats. Except as expressly stipulated by the central government, the provisions of these measures shall apply; 2. To avoid practical obstacles and facilitate the procedures for donation collection venues, receipts will be waived; 3. The above-mentioned relief donations shall be collected and reported by the respective movie theaters, theaters, and entertainment venues, and a stamp indicating "relief donation received" shall be affixed to the tickets. If only seat prices are charged without issuing tickets, the calculation shall be based on the actual seat prices; 4. The relief donations collected by each movie theater, theater, and entertainment venue shall be settled once a day, and a form shall be filled out every ten days, together with the donations, and reported to the respective tax collection offices for verification and collection. The form for the ten-day report will be determined separately; 5. The respective tax collection offices shall submit the above-mentioned donations received to the bureau on the same day for remittance to the Central Bank for allocation; 6. The respective tax collection offices shall compile a summary table of the donation amounts reported by each movie theater, theater, and entertainment venue every ten days, and submit it to the bureau for verification; 7. Each movie theater, theater, and entertainment venue shall collect and remit relief donations honestly. If the respective tax collection offices believe that the amount of donations reported by the collection venues does not match their business income, they may inspect the essential books of the venue. If concealment or underreporting is discovered, it shall be reported for handling according to law; 8. If there are any matters not covered by these measures, they shall be amended at any time; 9. These measures shall be implemented after being approved by the Municipal Government.

The Telephone Bureau Establishes a Pudong Branch

Inter-Concession Telephone Service to be Signed Soon

Restoration of Wusong Telephone Service to Begin Soon

A reporter from the Huadong News Agency interviewed Mr. Yu Bingjian, Chief Engineer of the Telephone Bureau, yesterday. The various topics discussed are recorded separately below:

Inter-Concession Telephone Service to be Signed

The contract reform for the Inter-Concession Telephone Service has been agreed upon by the company, approved by the Public Works Department, and the French Concession authorities have no objections to this contract. Therefore, the contract can be signed soon by the Bureau, the Public Utilities Bureau, and the company. The location of the signing has not yet been determined.

Restoration of Wusong Telephone Service to Begin

Regarding the restoration of the Wusong telephone service, the Bureau decided to restore it for the convenience of traffic in Songzhen because the Bureau repeatedly received letters from Tongji University and other organizations in Wusong requesting it. The required materials have been prepared, and workers will be dispatched tomorrow to install the equipment. Initially, 50 telephones will be installed temporarily for use by Tongji University and businesses. The service is expected to be fully operational in about a month. As for whether a fee will be charged for calls between Wusong and Shanghai after completion, the Wusong Telephone Company used to charge long-distance rates. The Bureau now intends to waive the fee according to the city telephone regulations to promote its popularity. This point has been reported to the Ministry of Communications for instructions, and it can be confirmed before the service is opened.

Establishment of the Pudong Branch

When the Bureau built a new building in Northern Chanzu the year before last, it also built a Pudong branch in Lanni Ferry in Pudong. It has long been completed and currently stores materials and other items. Preparations are being made to establish the Pudong branch as soon as possible. In the future, telephones for users in Pudong can be directly connected through the Pudong branch. If they are calling to Puxi, the Pudong branch will connect to the Nanshi General Bureau and then connect. As for the telephone machines installed across the boundary by the existing Pudong Telephone Company, they can be resolved at the same time as the Inter-Concession Telephone Service is signed.

Automatic Telephone Exchange

In addition, since the city began converting to automatic exchanges, the work has been progressing rapidly. 60 machines can be replaced every day. In the Nanshi area, the replacement can be completely completed in about a week, and then the replacement of machines in the Zhabei area will continue. However, the telephone poles and wires in the Zhabei area were mostly damaged by the January 28th Incident, so the poles and wires must be reinstalled at the same time. The automatic exchange is expected to be operational by the end of the month.

But the Huzhou Route is Delayed Until Today Due to Ice

The Jiangzhe Inland River Peace Steamship Company closed its accounts for the 21st year. Samsung Factory is commendable for putting the overall interest first. In addition to keeping the letter of apology in the association for future reference, we are sending ten pieces of Melton fabrics with this letter. Please check and issue a receipt for the use of supporting the Righteous Army."

The Wood and Lumber Industry in the French Concession Opposes the Sanitation Tax

| Industry Called a Meeting Yesterday to Oppose |

The wood and lumber businesses in the French Concession recently received a notice from the French police to pay a sanitation tax. They convened a meeting of the industry yesterday afternoon at 2 p.m. at the Fourth District Branch of the Citizens' Federation at No. 18 Xinle Lane, Nanyang Bridge, to oppose it. More than 20 businesses, including Tongxing, Chengda, Lixing, Maosheng, Wanfeng, and Yinji, attended. Wang Shenghang was publicly elected as chairman, and he reported that the French police recently sent police officers to notify each household to pay a classified business tax, and that there had been instances of unreasonable punishment at the Songshan Road police station. This industry has never had this tax, so it is difficult to accept. He requested a public decision on the measures. It was decided that: 1. A temporary office of the United Association of Wood and Lumber Industry in the French Concession would be established; 2. Lin Zhengtang, Huang Zhixian, Yu Xinrui, Wang Shengfang, and Xu Kaijun would be elected as representatives responsible for the negotiations; 3. All businesses would be notified to unanimously oppose and deny it; 4. An investigation would be conducted to collect penalty slips if any businesses had been penalized, so that it would be easier to negotiate; 5. A joint letter would be sent to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association in the French Concession, the Second District Citizens' Federation, and the Shanghai Wood Industry Association to negotiate reasonably for the cancellation of the extortionate tax; 6. Representatives would be sent to petition the Chinese directors if necessary. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Nanyang Maru Incident: Investigation of Opium Dispute

The Nisshin Kisen Co., Ltd.'s Yangtze River steamer Nanyang Maru, arriving in Shanghai from Hankou, experienced a dispute over the search for opium. The details are as follows:

Strict Opium Inspection: When Yangtze River ships arrive in Shanghai, the Shanghai Opium Suppression Bureau often sends plainclothes inspectors on board to search for smuggled opium. All six company vessels are subject to inspection. Last month, a China Merchants Steam Navigation Company ship was set on fire and its crew assaulted during an inspection. Previously, the Nisshin Kisen Company's Yangtze River ship Xiangyang Maru was also boarded and searched, but nothing was found.

Searching the Nanyang: On January 30th, the Nisshin Kisen's Nanyang Maru arrived in Shanghai from Hankou and docked at the company's pier. At that time, fourteen plainclothes opium suppression inspectors arrived on board. Many of the crew members were absent. The inspectors immediately entered the cabins to conduct a search. The ship's stewards and others came forward to stop them. The inspectors identified themselves, stating that they were inspectors and wanted to search the fire room. However, the ship's stewards and others strongly refused.

Sounding the Alarm: The inspectors insisted on searching the engine room and fire room, but the ship's personnel still refused them entry. While they were arguing, the personnel on board accused the inspectors of being imposters and grabbed a bronze gong from the cabin, sounding it loudly to call for help. Upon hearing the gong, the inspectors left the ship and went ashore.

Police Capture: When the alarm was sounded in the main cabin, Japanese crew members on the bridge raised a flag. The water police immediately arrived in a small boat and boarded the Nanyang Maru. By this time, all the inspectors had left except for one who was apprehended for being slower than the others. In addition to this, an engine-related item was also inspected. The crew pointed out that the person captured was a rogue who disguised himself as an inspector. The water police have already taken the captured person to the station for questioning.

Shanghai-Taiwan Shipping Route to Extend to Huangyan

The five vessels of the Lian'an Shipping Bureau in Shanghai, operating on the Shanghai-Taiwan route – Zhoushan, Daxing, Chuanshan, Dahua, and Taizhou – currently run from Shanghai as the starting point to Haimen, Taizhou Prefecture, Zhejiang Province, as the destination. It is now reported that the bureau, responding to the needs of the people of Huangyan and the requests of local gentry and merchants, plans to assign one of the five vessels to extend the route to Huangyan, so that passengers and cargo from Huangyan traveling to Shanghai will not have to transfer ships at Haimen.

Promulgation of Registration Rules for Dock Porters Handling Passenger Luggage

Yesterday, the Shanghai Municipal Government promulgated the "Shanghai Municipal Registration Rules for Dock Porters Handling Passenger Luggage." (Article 1) All porters at docks in this city who handle passenger luggage as a business must apply for registration with the Public Security Bureau, in accordance with the regulations of the Shanghai South Shipping Public Affairs Bureau for the management of docks. (Article 2) Porters applying for registration must first obtain five copies of the registration application form from the Public Security Bureau (one copy to be kept by the Social Affairs Bureau, two copies by the Public Security Bureau, and two copies by the Public Affairs Bureau), and submit them together with two 2.5-inch head-and-shoulder photos to the Public Affairs Bureau and Social Affairs Bureau for review and approval. (Article 3) Dock porters handling passenger luggage who have passed the review and received the approval notice must, within seven days, personally bring a registration fee of one silver dollar and a stamp fee of one dime to the Public Security Bureau to obtain a registration certificate and uniform style. (Article 4) Porters must wear their uniform and carry their registration certificate when working, so that they can be inspected by officers and police from the Public Security, Public Affairs, and Social Affairs Bureaus at any time. Before handling passenger luggage, they must first show their registration certificate to the passenger for verification. (Article 5) If a passenger does not want to hire a porter, the porter must not forcibly take the luggage or extort money. (Article 6) The price for porters handling passenger luggage is as follows, calculated in silver dollars: small items, 5 cents; medium items, 10 cents; large items, 15 cents. (Article 7) When a porter ceases to operate, they must submit their registration certificate to the Public Security Bureau for cancellation; otherwise, the guarantor will be responsible for recovering it. (Article 8) If a porter loses their registration certificate, they must report it to the Public Security Bureau and apply for a replacement, and also publish a statement in the newspaper declaring it invalid. (Article 9) Registration certificates must not be lent or substituted; violators will have their registration certificates revoked. (Article 10) Porters' registration certificates must be submitted to the Public Security Bureau for renewal every July. (Article 11) Those who violate the provisions of Articles 1, 5, and 10 will be subject to detention for up to 15 days or a fine of up to 15 yuan. In more serious cases, their registration certificates will be revoked. (Article 12) Matters not fully covered in these rules may be submitted for amendment at any time. (Article 13) These rules will be implemented from the date of approval by the Municipal Government. Three registration principles: (1) Priority will be given to porters who are already handling luggage at the docks for initial registration. (2) The operating locations of each registered porter will be specified; those who originally operated at a certain dock must continue to operate at that dock to avoid confusion. (3) The number of registered porters will be limited to avoid oversupply and competition for business.

Municipal Health Bureau Urges Slum Dwellers to Get Vaccinated Quickly

Don't Spend a Cent

It's to Prevent Smallpox

The Municipal Health Bureau issued a notice yesterday urging slum dwellers to get vaccinated quickly, saying, "Smallpox is a contagious disease. If contracted, it can lead to death in severe cases, and blindness or pockmarks in mild cases. To prevent smallpox, get vaccinated quickly. There are over 20,000 slum dwellings in Shanghai, housing over 150,000 people, most of whom are laborers. Because they are busy making a living, they neglect vaccination. By the time they develop smallpox, it will be too late to regret. This Bureau is aware of this situation, so it is sending doctors to vaccinate you, without charging you a cent. This is solely to prevent smallpox and protect your health. Please do not misunderstand. When the doctors come, do not be afraid. Come forward for vaccination. This Bureau has also asked the police from each district of the Public Security Bureau to provide care and inform everyone about vaccination. Please do not misunderstand the good intentions of this Bureau."

The Traffic Departments of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou Railways, which had classified rush for transportation as a second-class item according to the railway's general freight classification table, have now, in order to protect agricultural products, changed it to a fourth-class item for freight collection, effective from February 1st, to reduce the burden on farmers.

Telegraph Bureau Implements City Telephone Transmission and Receipt of Telegrams Under Ministry Order

｜Special Line Telephone Installation May Be Requested for Communication｜

Since Zhu Jia-hua took office as Minister of Communications, he has been actively and gradually seeking to improve the national telegraph business. In addition to instructing the telegraph bureau to use telephone numbers as the address of the recipient and already implementing this yesterday, he yesterday ordered the bureau to implement two methods: using telephones to transmit telegrams and studying the national pronunciation telegraph code, and limited the implementation to starting today. The details of the methods are recorded as follows:

Implementing Three Methods: According to Hua Jinghan, Section Chief of the Business Section of the Telegraph Bureau, in order to facilitate telegrams, the Ministry of Communications specially ordered this Bureau to implement three methods of improvement: (1) Using telephone numbers as the address of the recipient. This measure was implemented today (i.e., yesterday), and senders have already come to send telegrams. (2) Using telephones to transmit telegrams. This Bureau only received the order yesterday and is also scheduled to implement it starting today (methods recorded later). (3) Studying the national pronunciation telegraph code. This method uses one, two, or three words of the national pronunciation to replace the original numerical code for each character. This Bureau is currently studying it, but due to various reasons, it is difficult to implement it immediately. As for the implementation period, it will be no earlier than mid-April or May of this year.

Ministry of Communications Instructions: The Bureau received instructions from the Ministry of Communications yesterday, stating, "In order to comply with the matter, the Ministry has formulated a method for sending and receiving telegrams by city telephone in order to facilitate public communication and increase the speed of telegrams. Now, 100 copies of the method, along with blank application forms and registration books, are sent to the bureau for compliance. This order."

Abstract of the Method: The method for sending and receiving telegrams by city telephone has a total of fourteen articles. The key points are recorded below: (1) Telephone users who wish to have telegrams sent from other places transmitted by telephone from the local telegraph bureau or radio station (hereinafter referred to as "Bureau") or who wish to have telegrams sent to other places transmitted to the Bureau by telephone must obtain an application form from the Bureau, fill in the following items, and submit it with a registration fee of one silver dollar for registration with the Bureau: (A) Name and detailed address of the applicant; (B) Telephone number installed; (C) Receiving or sending telegrams, or both; (D) Daily time for receiving or sending telegrams; (E) Code word; (2) After receiving the application form and registration fee, the Bureau should immediately issue a receipt, register the items opened in the application form in the registration book, verify the start date, and reply to the applicant for verification; (3)(4) omitted; (5) No additional handling fee will be charged for telegrams sent and received by telephone; (6) Those who wish to send telegrams by telephone must prepay a deposit sufficient for half a month's telegram fees, which will be determined by the Bureau. When the deposit is about to be used up, the Bureau will notify the sender in writing to continue depositing. If the deposit has been used up and not continued, the Bureau may stop receiving telegrams; (7) Before receiving or sending telegrams by telephone, the recipient or sender (hereinafter referred to as "recipient and sender") must report their name or business name and inform the Bureau of the agreed code word for verification. The code word should be kept strictly confidential by both the recipient and sender and the Bureau, and may be replaced by the recipient and sender by notifying the Bureau in writing when necessary to prevent impersonation; (8) When transmitting telegrams on the telephone, Chinese telegrams should read out the telegraph code one by one, and foreign telegrams should read out the letters one by one. However, for the convenience of the other party in identifying, the telegraph code and letters may be transmitted according to the following reading method when necessary (reading method omitted); (9)(10) omitted; (11) When the Bureau cannot transmit telegrams quickly by telephone for any reason, it should immediately seal the telegram, note the reason, and deliver it by messenger; (12) Recipients and senders may contact the Bureau to install a dedicated telephone line for sending and receiving telegrams, and the cost will be borne by the recipient and sender; (13) Those who agree with the Bureau to send

Record of the Annual Meeting of the Chinese Leprosy Relief Association

=Speech by Director of Health Bureau Li Ting'an=

=Election of Yan Fuqing and Others as Directors=

The Chinese Leprosy Relief Association has been established for seven years and has been very active in leprosy relief work. The association held its seventh annual meeting yesterday afternoon at 4:30 in the Zhongshan Hall on the fifth floor of the YMCA on Bowuyuan Road. The details of the meeting are recorded below:

Attendees

The attendees included Kuang Fu-zhao, Chen Yongfan, Cheng Lian, Wu Liande, Diao Xinde, Wu Weide, Ou Weiguo, Mrs. Cai Bingjiu, Wang Zhiren, Chen Wenying, Liu Liqian, Yan Fuqing, and representatives from the Social Affairs Bureau Chen Lengseng, representatives from the City Party Department He Yuanming, and over thirty other people.

Work Report

After the meeting was announced, the chairman of the association, Li Yuanxin, delivered a welcome speech. Next, the general secretary of the association, Wu Zhijian, reported on the progress of the work in the past year, saying that in recent years, the Yangtze River flood and the two major incidents of September 18th and January 28th were unprecedented events in history and had a great impact on the work of the association. The leprosy relief work from July 20th to December 21st is briefly reported below: (1) The Hongkou Skin Hospital, sponsored by the association, treats leprosy patients two days a week, with 135 leprosy patients. The director is Dr. Chen Hongkang, and the annual expenditure is 4,000 yuan. When the January 28th Incident occurred, the hospital was located in the war zone, and doctors and nurses were sent to join the temporary Red Cross to rescue the wounded soldiers. (2) A new hospital will be opened on Qiongnan Island, Guangdong, in cooperation with the local Chamber of Commerce, and houses are currently being built, which will be completed soon. (3) Luoding County, Guangdong, is the hometown of Cai Tingkai, the commander-in-chief of the 19th Route Army. Dr. Dick founded a hospital there seven or eight years ago, but it was small in scale. The association now bears half of the funding each year. (4) In Qingyuan County, Guangdong, the customs are very strange. Anyone with leprosy must be driven onto a boat and cannot go ashore for life. The church pastor Wu Yinte has operated a relief boat, but the equipment is not complete. After I went to inspect it, a base has been purchased and a hospital will be built soon to accommodate leprosy patients. (5) The address of the Xiamen branch has been allocated over 100 mu of land by the Siming County Construction Bureau and will be built soon. The president of the association, Dr. Lin Wenqing, the president of Xiamen University, is making great efforts to raise funds. (6) The Nanchang branch is the first branch established by the association, with a history of over two years of operating a hospital. A new auditorium and workshop have been built for leprosy patients to gather for work and it is planned to purchase land to add wards to accommodate 60 people. (7) Last Christmas, the association donated a total of 7,839 yuan to widely provide relief to leprosy patients in various provinces. (8) From October 5th to 6th, the association convened a national leprosy conference at the Lister Institute, and representatives from the United Kingdom and the United States were sent to attend the conference. The results of the conference included three items: (A) A request was submitted to the Ministry of Health to formulate national leprosy regulations, which the Ministry has now begun to draft, and the association's written opinions have been prepared and submitted; (B) A request was submitted to the Ministry of Education to include leprosy teaching materials in textbooks at all levels, and the Ministry has notified the National Education Office to order various bookstores to compile them; (C) Drugs for leprosy relief in the Philippine Islands are very effective, and the conference decided to adopt them. The Governor of the Philippines has promised to supply them as much as possible, and they will be transported to Shanghai soon and distributed throughout the country to provide relief to leprosy compatriots. As for future plans, special attention will be paid to the number of items in the five-year plan for leprosy relief and actively carried out. I will go to inspect Jiangbei and other places in Hunan within the month and build hospitals again.

Li's Speech

Next, Dr. Li Ting'an, Director of the Municipal Health Bureau, gave a speech, saying, "Today is the seventh annual meeting of the Chinese Leprosy Relief Association, and I am very honored to attend. The association has the research of experts from all over the world on leprosy relief, so I don't need to say more. In my opinion, leprosy is the most terrible disease, and it often does not forgive patients, driving them out to drift and make a living, which is very pitiful. According to the survey and statistics of the national expert Mr. Wu Liande, there are more than one million leprosy patients in our country, and the relief problem is very serious. I often read your association's monthly magazine as a reference, including the five-year plan for leprosy relief, such as (1) making a detailed leprosy survey, (2) compiling the facts of leprosy into teaching materials for schools, (3) participating in urban sanitation campaigns in various places, (4) organizing the Central Leprosy Association, (5) convening national leprosy conferences, (6) urging the government to promulgate leprosy laws, (7) building at least one leprosy hospital in each province with leprosy, (8) having at least one leprosy treatment center in major cities, (9) holding a national student elimination of leprosy speech contest every year, (10) finding ways to protect and cultivate leprosy children (11) arranging for the resettlement of cured leprosy patients, etc. I am very admired. Hearing the report of Mr. Wu Zhijian, General Secretary of the association, and the results of the efforts to promote it, I have to express some feelings. Everyone thinks that the government does not cooperate with leprosy relief and expresses dissatisfaction. After investigating, there are many diseases in our country, chronic diseases such as tuberculosis, lung disease, trachoma, venereal disease, leprosy, and acute diseases such as cholera, scarlet fever, diphtheria, etc., and the scope is very large. The Health Bureau focuses on public health and cannot specialize in a certain disease. Also, because the finances are very tight, it cannot subsidize the progress. I believe that in the future, when the health cause is developed, the government and the leprosy problem will be able to cooperate and pay attention to relief work. I also express my sympathy for your association and wish your association to continue its efforts, and hope that citizens, medical circles, and health circles will cooperate and carry out the work together. I am very fortunate."

Election of Directors

The report on the income and expenditure status of the past year and the budget for the 22nd year was given, and Dr. Lewis gave a speech. Finally, new directors were elected. The elected were Yan Fuqing, Li Yuanxin, Kuang Fuzhuo, Diao Xinde, Cheng Lian, Zhu Shaoping, Wu Liande, Wang Zhiren, Gu Enkang, Li Guansen, Ding Shujing, Mrs. Xiao Zhigu, Li Yaobang, Luo Yunyan, and Ms. Yan Feisha, and fifteen others. The meeting was adjourned for refreshments.

Garrison Headquarters Executes Two Kidnappers by Firing Squad

The Songhu Garrison Headquarters executed two kidnappers by firing squad at Longhua Airport yesterday morning (the 1st). Its announcement said, "For the announcement of the case, according to the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, Chen Tianbiao and two other criminals involved in the kidnapping and extortion of the young child of Zheng Weisheng's family at Miaojitou outside the West Gate of Longshan, Zhenhai County on the night of the first day of the fourth lunar month of last year were arrested at 14 Ruifu Lane, Caishi Road, this port and sent to the department. After interrogation, it was clearly determined that Chen Tianbiao (i.e., Chen Tianbiao i.e., Lao Chen, also known as Chen Junyao, also known as Zhang Zhongkui) and Hu Yuqi had jointly committed the act of kidnapping and extorting ransom. According to Article 1, Paragraph 1 of the Provisional Regulations for the Punishment of Bandits and Robbers, each was sentenced to death. The criminal Chen Tianbiao and two others were identified, tied to the execution ground, and executed by firing squad to show warning. This announcement. The executed kidnappers were Chen Tianbiao, 36 years old, from Ningbo, and Hu Yuqi, 28 years old, from Ningbo."

French Concession Police Crack Down on Roulette Gambling Den

Established by a Frenchman

Gamblers of all nationalities involved

The French Concession authorities have long strictly prohibited gambling within the concession, but recently a Frenchman named Hairbo (transliteration) initiated the establishment of a roulette gambling den in a large house at No. 803 Foch Road in the French Concession, gathering crowds to gamble. The operation was discovered by Fabre (transliteration), the chief inspector of the French Concession Police, who, on the morning of January 31st (the day before yesterday) at 4:00 AM, led Western detectives Xie Zhengtiao, Zhang Wenliang, Fang Zhaolin, Zhang Dongcheng, Dai Rongji, Bai Xiuzheng, Xu Wen Shao Kong Qing Tong, and other patrol officers. They disguised themselves as gamblers and entered the premises. At a prearranged signal, they apprehended all the gamblers without a single one escaping. The arrestees included the den owner Hairbo, Chinese dealers Lin Fengzhang, Shen Changsheng, Zhou Heshun, employees Wang Liansheng, Xu Amao, Zhou Shihong, Zhu Ade, Pan Xianglin, Ling Shuqing, Zhou Amao, Dai Jinfang, Weng Shiren, and nine foreign gamblers of American, French, Portuguese, and other nationalities. Two roulette wheels (one upstairs and one downstairs), a box of chips, several hundred dollars in gambling funds, ledgers, and other items were seized. All were taken to the police station, where the chief inspector interrogated each person. The foreign nationals were handed over to their respective consulates for further investigation, while the Chinese were temporarily detained. Yesterday afternoon at 12:00 PM, Lin and the other eleven Chinese were sent to the Second Special District Court, where Judge Zhang Chaozuo presided over the second criminal court for the trial. The police lawyer, Gu Shouxi, presented the case, stating that the police needed to conduct further investigation, and requesting the court to postpone the hearing to a later date. When questioned, Lin Fengzhang confessed to being a dealer at the den after being introduced by a certain Westerner and stated that he had only been working there for five or six days. Shen Changsheng and Zhou Heshun similarly confessed that they had been invited to gamble the previous evening by a Westerner they knew, lost several tens of dollars, and were then arrested. They denied helping with the gambling and begged for leniency. Wang Liansheng and the other nine people all claimed to be coolies and servants. Judge Zhang reviewed the confessions and ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody for a further hearing on the 8th of this month.

Public Concession Police Crack Down on Nine Gambling Dens

| 104 Gamblers Arrested |

The Public Concession Police Department, recognizing that during the Lunar New Year holiday, some scoundrels often take advantage of hotels and teahouses to gather crowds for gambling and profit from skimming, issued a special order to all police stations to strictly investigate and crack down on such activities. The day before yesterday, Chief Inspector Yao Jialin of District C, along with Head Constable Herhua, Detectives He Lianzhen, Sun Dafa, and others, cracked down on nine gambling dens. A total of 104 gamblers were arrested, most of whom were playing Pai Gow. Yesterday morning, police lawyer Qian Xunjiu prosecuted them in the First Special Court on charges of gambling according to the criminal law. After Judge Zhang Junqing interrogated and verified the facts, he sentenced them to fines as a warning. The details of the gambling dens are listed below: ⑴ The Old Zha Police Station arrested sixteen gamblers including Wu Jinbao, Song Zhidi, Pan Azhen, Hu Liusheng, Lu Jinkang, Shen Changfa, Jin Gaosheng, Luo Ahui, and Zhang Asi at the Great Shanghai Restaurant at No. 348 Tianjin Road, Room 530. ⑵ The Hongkou Police Station arrested five people including Ou Zhenxiong, Zhu Xingtao, Liu Luyou, and Zhou Ganquan at No. 50 Tongde Lane, Zhapu Road. ⑶ They also arrested four people including Wang Shunren, Zhang Zixiang, Guo Qiang, and Tian Zilin at No. 108 Yuanchang Road. ⑷ They also arrested eight people including Zhong Acheng, Lu Yi, Wang Quan, Peng Jiu, Liu Qiang, and Wang He at No. 608 Renzhi Lane, North Sichuan Road. ⑸ The Huishi Police Station arrested eight people including Zhao Bolin, Wu Mugen, Zhang Yueliang, Xiao Agui, Yu Tingyang, and Liu Zengtang at No. 50 Anle Hotel, No. 439 North Zhejiang Road. ⑹ The Yulin Road Police Station arrested fourteen people including Qiu Heshang, Wang Xianghuai, Shang Baoshou, Chen Jiqing, and Jiang Jinji at No. 102 Ford Road. ⑺ They also arrested twenty-four people including Liu Asheng, Fang Aer, Shi Hongfu, Zhou Yunsheng, and Xu Huishan at Nos. 1145-1147 Huade Road. ⑻ They also arrested eleven people including Xu Caiying, Liu Xinqi, Qi Xiangting, and Zhao Liangcai at No. 461 Yangshupu Road. ⑼ They also arrested fourteen people including Zhang Axing, Wang Chuting, Xie Laotai, Jiang Yongren, Liu Ajin, Wu Linsheng, and Liu Yuying at No. 23 Huade Road. After this strict crackdown by the police, it is hoped that the gambling trend may be slightly curbed.

Telephone Numbers Replace Recipient Addresses

Starting yesterday (the 1st), in major cities with telephones, such as Nanjing, Shanghai, Wuhan, Tianjin, Beiping, Qingdao, Suzhou, Shantou, Jiangwan, Nanxiang, Longhua, Xiangshan, Tangshan, Mu Du, Wuhu, Shashi, Jingzhou, Jiujiang, and Guling, telephone subscribers can register with the telegraph office to use their telephone number as the recipient's address. After this, when a telegram arrives with the same telephone number, it can be delivered to the recipient, and the telegram does not need to include street or house numbers. However, the recipient's name must still be added after the registration to avoid errors. The previous method of telegram registration will still be used as usual and will not be abolished.

Rickshaw Puller Beats Female Passenger to Death

All for a single dime

Taking a life

At around 11:00 PM last night, at the intersection of Avenue Joffre and Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession, a young woman, about twenty years old, wearing a black silk cotton qipao and a gray patriotic cloth jacket, rode in a small rickshaw. When the rickshaw reached the intersection, she asked the rickshaw puller to stop, then slowly got out and handed him a dime for the fare. However, the rickshaw puller noticed that the dime was a "human head" coin and wanted to exchange it. The woman had already crossed the road and reached the Dongxin Bridge. The rickshaw puller ran up to her and tried to grab her velvet collar. The woman turned around and grabbed the rickshaw puller, and a fight broke out. It is unknown how, but the woman was beaten in a vital area by the rickshaw puller and fell to the ground, dead. A patrolman from the Old Zha Police Station No.

City Investigation Team Arrests Wartime Traitor Who Fled Shanghai

During the January 28th Incident last year, a traitor named Li Xiaowuzi from Funing colluded with many bandits to go to Zhabei, willingly joined the enemy, killed our armed anti-Japanese soldiers, set fire to civilian houses, looted indiscriminately, raped women, and committed all kinds of evils. After the ceasefire agreement was reached, Li knew things were not good for him and fled, remaining at large. Although the authorities issued a strict arrest warrant, he was not apprehended. It is now known that the Military Affairs Commission secretly ordered the Songhu Garrison Headquarters to instruct the Shanghai Public Security Bureau Director Wen Hongen to arrest and punish Li. After receiving the order, Director Wen instructed the investigation team to make a strict arrest. The day before yesterday, it was discovered that Li was hiding at No. 109 Hefeng Lane, Bailinan Road, Caojiadu, West Shanghai. The team dispatched a large number of detectives including Chen Liangfu and Wang Yixin, along with Patrol Officer Gu Wentao from the Sixth District Sub-Bureau, and led police officers to Li's house at 5:30 AM yesterday morning. They rushed into Li's house from both the front and back doors and arrested Li. According to his confession, his name is Ji Xiaowuzi, he is 38 years old, from Funing, and he lives at No. 109 Hefeng Lane, Bailinan Road. He is a recruiting agent and factory inspector at the Ri-Hua Cotton Mill on Route Robert, with a monthly salary of 30 yuan, and he has been doing this for nine years. The rest of his confession was evasive. Captain Lu considered the case to be serious and ordered Li to be detained for strict interrogation.

42 arrived at the scene and arrested the rickshaw puller. The police handed him over to the court this morning for punishment. The corpse was sent to Renji Hospital and then transferred to the coroner's office for examination.

Total amount of customs gold unit convertible note reserve fund: 425,000 yuan, including 170,000 US dollars deposited with peer banks in this city, valued at 40 cents per customs gold unit, totaling 425,000 yuan. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Note Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. January 31, 1933, Central Bank Board of Supervisors.

Reader Consultation

What is China's problem?

| Mr. Shen Zuguang's letter seen in yesterday's column |

Reply: I have read your letter several times, and it is quite difficult to answer because what you are saying and what we are thinking about every day are at least two centuries apart, or like being in the tropics and exchanging pleasantries with a person from the North Pole. I simply don't know where to start. This is the first reason. You lack horizontal knowledge of modern political theory and its history. If I were to answer, I would have to start from the beginning. This is the second reason. Even if I analyze your original text, its main points are mostly vague and lack definite concepts, making it difficult to understand. As the ancients said, "If my own status is not clear, how can I worship my mother-in-law?" If I really answer, it would be like a donkey's lips not matching a horse's mouth, and the answer would not address the question. This is the third reason. Now, I will first discuss the points you raised in your original letter. After I receive your definite and further reply, I will conduct a detailed discussion. (1) Your letter says: "Everything succeeds with preparation, and fails without it." China's reforms in the past twenty-two years have always gone wrong because they have fallen into the trap of "just doing things first and then seeing what happens." The overthrow of the Qing Dynasty and the establishment of the Republic of China, while formally beginning in 1911, actually had its roots in the anti-Qing movements and theories of the Ming Dynasty loyalists after the Qing Dynasty entered the customs. After the Opium War, there was the Taiping Rebellion. In this revolutionary struggle, the most important democratic tasks were put on the agenda. During the Boxer Rebellion, the Boxers rose up to resist imperialism. Although they advocated "Support the Qing, destroy the foreigners," their violent resistance not only dealt a heavy blow to the imperialists but also posed a great threat to the Qing government. Although both of these revolutions failed, the Qing court had no choice but to open schools, abolish the imperial examination system, promote industry, and train new armies. As revolutionary movements brewed for a long time in various places, the struggle between anti-Manchu thought and monarchism became very intense. The people of the country, seeing the Qing court's incompetence, turned to yearn for revolution. By the time of the 1911 Revolution, all provinces followed suit. This kind of mutual influence and continuous growth has been going on for almost three hundred years. Can it still be considered "without preparation"? In your opinion, what kind of "preparation" is needed? What are you "preparing" for? Is it truly like the Qing court's so-called "preparation for constitutionalism"? Moreover, we know that the plans for improving or changing the lives of an individual, a family, a locality, or a country are never conceived by some great men or celebrities who close their doors and fantasize. Instead, they are formed in actual struggles, experiencing the current needs, and thus taking shape. The problem with the Chinese people now is not the lack of planning or "preparation," but the fundamental lack of "doing." Take the War of Resistance against Japan, for example. We hear every day that we have the determination to resist Japan, but in fact, there is no determination at all. We hear every day that we have made sufficient preparations, but in fact, there are no preparations at all. We hear every day about long-term resistance, but where is the reality? Your so-called "just doing things first and then seeing what happens" is actually the opposite of the truth! No matter what the matter is, planning only comes after doing. Planning and preparation are part of the process of doing. Without doing, planning and preparation become empty talk to deceive people. On this point, you have already made the mistake of reversing cause and effect. (2) Your letter raises a question: "What is a good country? What is a good government?" This is indeed a very important question. Your answer is "Everyone in the country lives in peace and prosperity." This is wrong. Throughout the world, past and present, it is impossible to find a good country and a good government where "everyone lives in peace and prosperity." You can only give this kind of irrelevant answer to this question because you don't first explain what a country is and how to explain its goodness or badness. You don't first explain what a government is and how to explain its goodness or badness. Let me be blunt: it's not that you haven't explained what a country or government is, but that you haven't fundamentally understood what a country is and what a government is. That's why you say things like "The reason for the establishment of a country..." Once you go wrong on this path, you will always be wrong. (3) Your letter also says, "In the past twenty-two years, China has tried all kinds of political systems, but none of them have been successful." This is even more wrong! What exactly are the so-called "various systems"? Where exactly have they been "tried"? To be honest, we have all been through the tides of the 1898 Reforms, the Eight-Nation Alliance, the 1911 Revolution, and Hong Xian's imperial dream. Tell me, what exactly are these "various systems"? (4) Your letter says, "Every country has its own history, human nature, customs, and habits." This is another "Four Harmony Soup" statement. What is called "Four Harmony Soup"? Some incompetent doctors, when diagnosing a patient, cannot determine the true source of the patient's illness and dare not prescribe real medicine. Therefore, they always prescribe "licorice, ledebouriella, schizonepeta, and dwarf lilyturf root" for people to eat, which is called Four Harmony Soup. Although the patient cannot be cured by eating it, it will not make the illness worse (in fact, it is an incompetent doctor killing people), just to perfunctorily deceive money. A group of dull-minded people always talk about "history, human nature, customs, and habits." But I want to ask: What is history? What is human nature? What are customs and habits? How are they produced? If you cannot explain their origins, then you should keep your mouth shut and study them first. (5) Your letter says, "China should have a constitutional monarchy, and the warlord conflicts in the past and present might be less common." You are advocating for a constitutional monarchy. However, you also say, "I think any organization with power, whether large or small, is better off with a dictatorship. Although America is a republic, its president is a dictator, and the Secretary of State is nothing more than his staff. Mussolini in Italy and Stalin in Russia are both dictators." You are also advocating for "personal dictatorship." What exactly is "dictatorship"? The British constitutional monarchy is certainly not a personal dictatorship, but it is not suspended in the air. It has its own social foundation, that is, a class or a group. As for Stalin in Russia and Mussolini in Italy, although they are said to be personal dictatorships, their dictatorships are vastly different. They each have their own class background. The Russian political system is a proletarian dictatorship, that is, a proletarian dictatorship. The so-called "Stalin" dictatorship is just a short-term historical process in the initial stage of the proletarian dictatorship. Mussolini's dictatorship is nothing more than a representative of fascism, that is, a very right-wing, extremely reactionary bourgeois dictatorship. There is no such thing as a purely personal dictatorship without a mass base. The difference between Stalin and Mussolini is like the difference between heaven and earth. You are putting them all together and smelting them in the same furnace, which shows that you seem to lack analytical skills. (To be continued tomorrow)

Education News

Important News

Jiangsu Education Department Bans Illegal Organizations

Jiangsu Agricultural Society and others unregistered

Circular issued to all counties to investigate and ban them

The Jiangsu Provincial Education Department issued a directive to all county magistrates regarding the ban on the unregistered Jiangsu Agricultural Society and other organizations, as ordered. The directive stated: "We have received Directive No. 521 from the Jiangsu Provincial Government, ordering compliance. It is ordered that the establishment of academic organizations must be approved by the provincial educational administrative authority to be legal. Now, there are so-called Jiangsu Agricultural Society, Chicken Farming Society, Bee Farming Society, Animal Husbandry Society, Jiangbei Salt Reclamation Promotion Association, Cultivation and Research Society, Jiangsu Rural Improvement Society, and other organizations. It should be investigated whether they have been approved and registered, in order to uphold the law. It is hereby ordered that the Department handle the matter and report back." After investigation, it was found that the Jiangsu Agricultural Society, Chicken Farming Society, Bee Farming Society, Animal Husbandry Society, Jiangbei Salt Reclamation Promotion Association, Cultivation and Research Society, Jiangsu Rural Improvement Society, etc., have not directly applied to this Department for approval and registration, nor have the relevant Education Bureaus forwarded applications for filing. The establishment of various cultural organizations is originally intended to promote academics and benefit the people, and this Department encourages it. However, those who establish such organizations must act in accordance with the law, and no procedures should be neglected. If, as mentioned above, the so-called Jiangsu Agricultural Society, etc., have not applied to the county for approval and registration, and have not been forwarded by the Education Bureau for filing with this Department, it is not in accordance with the law and should be immediately investigated and banned. In addition to reporting back to the Provincial Government, this order is hereby issued to the county governments to immediately investigate and ban the above-mentioned unregistered Jiangsu Agricultural Society and other illegal organizations and report back separately. This matter concerns the execution of an order to investigate and handle the matter, which must be handled properly and without delay or negligence. This order is issued."

Six Students from Jiangsu Middle School Develop Aviation Fever, Apply to Aviation School

| Four Admitted |

In the recent year, Suzhou Middle School has implemented strict training. Junior high school education has been completely Boy Scout-ized, with all organization and facilities based entirely on Boy Scout training. High school students are subjected to strict military training. Last year, the Training Supervision Department inspected the military training of major middle schools in Jiangnan, and the school achieved the highest score. It is reported that several of the school's graduates have served as heads of security regiments. Recently, when the Hangzhou Central Aviation School held examinations, five graduates of the school applied. Except for one person who failed due to a physical condition (color blindness) and was not able to take the exam, three people were admitted (Li Wenhao, Zhang Suokui, and Zhu Yuanfeng). At the same time, the school's secretary also took the exam and was admitted. The enthusiasm of the school's staff and students for aviation and their determination to save the country are admirable.

Recent Developments in Implementing School Hygiene in the City

Schools Should Establish School Health Rooms

City Education Bureau Stipulates Indoor Equipment

The city's school hygiene work, after discussions between the City Education Bureau and the Health Bureau, initially designated Gaoqiao, Zhabei, and Hunnan districts as school hygiene experimental zones. Clinics and dental clinics were established in each of these districts for students from various schools to seek treatment. The Health Bureau also dispatched personnel to various schools to conduct physical examinations and correct deficiencies. Additionally, the two bureaus jointly organized three school hygiene personnel training classes. All of these initiatives were implemented successively during the previous semester. To facilitate the implementation of hygiene work, the City Education Bureau also instructed schools to allocate rooms as school health rooms. The Education Bureau has stipulated the following regarding indoor equipment, which is now recorded below: One record sheet box, one first-aid medicine tree (provided by the Bureau), one rectangular table, one chair, one spittoon, one washbasin with stand, one soap dish, one towel, one waste water bucket, one square stool, one large kettle, one teapot, two teacups. The schools are expected to provide these items themselves.

China Cooperative Society Organizes Cooperative Research Class

The China Cooperative Society has spared no effort in promoting cooperative endeavors in recent years. Recently, in order to cultivate high-caliber practical talent for cooperation, the society has specially established a Cooperative Research Class. Anyone with a genuine interest in cooperation, possessing a specialized or senior high school education or above, and having two or more years of practical experience in operating a cooperative or serving as a guidance worker, or having three or more years of experience in social service, may submit a detailed resume and research category to the society for application. The Research Class takes guidance research as its training direction. The training method is divided into three stages: the first stage is the correspondence research period, the second stage is the research period under the guidance of an instructor, and the third stage is the internship period. Full-time instructors are all cooperative experts from the society. In addition, domestic economic experts are invited to serve as special mentors. The training period is set from four to six months. After the completion of the period, those who are deemed qualified by the instructor's assessment will be given a certificate of qualification. It is learned that the class committee held its first meeting on January 30th at the Shanghai Bank Club. Committee members present included Wu Juenong, Wang Zhixin, Hou Houpei, and Wang Shiying. In addition to discussing various important matters, Wang Zhixin was elected as chairman of the committee, Wang Shiying as the director of general affairs for the class, and Wu Juenong as the director of academic affairs. It is said that preparations are largely in place and recruitment advertisements will be published in the newspaper soon.

The Girls' Department of Huadong Middle School, located at the end of Baylor Road, west of Xieqiao in this city, is scheduled to start school today. Formal classes will begin on Monday. Sports

Good Phenomenon: Sports Have Reached the Hinterland

=Simao, a Remote Area in Southern Yunnan, Holds Sports Meet=

=Hundreds of Men and Women Participate in Track and Field and Ball Games=

|Lu Guofan and Ding Baochen Commended for Their Promotion|

Simao is located in remote southern Yunnan. Although it is the capital of the Sipu region, it is a remote and desolate area plagued by miasma. The population is sparse, and the market is bleak. It has long been unnoticed by the world. This year, Simao suddenly held a grand sports meet. The meeting was held for a total of four days, from January 1st to 4th of this year. There were field events, track events, and various ball games, such as basketball, football, team ball, and tennis. It is particularly commendable that women actually participated in basketball and tennis competitions. In addition to sports, there were also various dances, games, and national martial arts. Simao is a small town, and the people all live by farming. In recent years, due to the ravages of epidemics, the population has been decreasing. There are famines everywhere, and the city is desolate. During the few days of the meeting, tens of thousands of people were in the streets, gathering in the sports field to watch. There were also hundreds of athletes. The layout of the venue was also quite impressive. It is heard that this meeting was due to the promotion of Lu Guofan, the Director of Colonial Affairs of Sipu. He had held a sports meet in Puer in October of last year. This time, he went to inspect the border and first arrived in Simao, so this meeting was able to be held. Ding Baochen, the magistrate of Simao County, also made many plans and raised huge amounts of money, and the meeting was able to be held without any difficulties.

Hong Kong Tennis World Circumstances Xu Huipei Has Hope of Winning Championship

Nineteen-Year-Old Youth Group is the Future Champion

A Dark Horse, Lun Qiang's Only Rival

Lun Qiang Brothers Fear Few Rivals for the Doubles Championship

(Hong Kong Correspondence) The Hong Kong Lawn Tennis Championships are about to begin. Famous players from Hong Kong will participate to win the championship, such as the younger Lun Qiang, the older Lun Qiang, and Fen Qiao. However, the most eye-catching player, considered to be Hong Kong's future champion, is the nineteen-year-old Chinese youth Xu Huipei. The unanimous praise and similar observations from various parties are also a great hope for the future of Chinese tennis.

The Championship is About to Change Hands

In this tournament, the championship is likely to change hands, producing a new champion and a new leader, giving Hong Kong's tennis world a new look. The younger Lun Qiang SirdarRumjahn is the holder of the championship, but Xu Huipei, who was defeated by Shanghai veteran White in the previous inter-port competition, is seen as the younger Lun Qiang's strong rival. The singles are like this, and there are few who can compete with the Lun Qiang brothers in doubles.

Xu Huipei's Achievements

Xu Huipei was a dark horse in the inter-port competition, defeating Shanghai veteran White. His speed of shooting is unmatched in Hong Kong. The backhand is his masterpiece. In the recent past, he has never suffered any setbacks. Because of his easy success, there are many who worry about him, thinking that winning is easy and losing is easy. To be fair, if Xu is in the best situation, he can dare to say that there is no one in Hong Kong who can compete with him. If Xu wins the Hong Kong championship, his performance will be similar to his performance against White.

Fen Qiao and the Older Lun Qiang

Fen Qiao has won the championship for the past three years, but has always fallen short. This year, with Xu Huipei and the younger Lun Qiang ahead, there is probably no hope. As for the older Lun Qiang H.D.Rumjahn, he has been working hard for many years, but is still regarded as a non-tactical player. The results of his efforts still cannot change the outside world's observations. The older Lun Qiang is ranked third in Hong Kong, and his ball skills have indeed improved a lot. If he is lucky in the draw, he may be able to reach the final.

British Naval Commander Peck

Among the group of famous players, there is one more person who is noteworthy, the British Navy Commander Peck of the British warship Kent. Peck performed exceptionally well in a recent game against Fen Qiao, and also won against the younger Lun Qiang in a practice match with a score of two to one. His backhand is as good as Xu Huipei's. Peck must be one of the final eight.

Seven Pairings in Doubles

In doubles, the Lun Qiang brothers are naturally the strongest pair with the highest hopes. However, there are endless changes, and it is difficult to say for sure with so many strong rivals. The doubles pairings are as follows:

(1) Lun Qiang Brothers (2) Fen Qiao and Gorman (3) He Jialiu and Yu Wenjie (4) Xu Huipei and Wu Shiguang (5) Harry William (6) Peck and Shaw (7) Luo Wenhui and Kun Cu.

Shenbao National Goods Weekly

National Goods Forum

The Housewife's Responsibility

— Pan Yang

Housewives bear significant responsibilities within the family. All matters, big and small, converge upon them. They wield the power of choice over all daily necessities. Excluding abnormal families where authority is usurped, Chinese housewives are truly the commanders of the household. In large families, although wives can often discuss matters, most hold the view that it's not their place. Therefore, whoever assumes this important task is solely responsible for the seven daily essentials. As for small families, how can the heads of the household, exhausted from their occupations, possibly consult on every detail? Thus, housewives must shoulder the burden. The above describes the reality. As to whether women should leave the home and enter society, that remains a theoretical debate and is beyond the scope of this article, so it need not be discussed.

Currently, facts demonstrate that housewives, as masters of household life, occupy an important position as consumers. Therefore, in this national goods movement, housewives bear significant responsibility and mission. The severity of the national crisis and the huge trade deficit should serve as a warning to awaken us from our delusions. From the perspective of household economics, we should certainly not use expensive imported goods. Moreover, many emerging domestic products are much better than foreign goods, and some can replace them. Because we are Chinese, we should resolve to use domestic goods. From now on, do not patronize stores that promote imported goods; instead, frequent Chinese national goods companies.

In the past, people were dominated by the idea of worshipping foreign goods. Housewives – especially modern women – considered using foreign goods fashionable and beautiful. In reality, every country in the world regards using domestic goods as a virtue. Visiting Chinese national goods companies is glorious, spirited, and resolute. Once we understand this, housewives bearing significant responsibility should immediately strive to realize it without shirking their duty. Based on correct ideas, we should vigorously refute erroneous thinking. I love national goods, I use national goods, I buy national goods, and my conscience gains immense comfort. Who dares to say this is not beautiful, because it is a virtue!

Reversing the annual trade deficit of 500 million taels of silver is precisely the responsibility of us housewives. We should shoulder this significant responsibility without hesitation.

Four Major Tasks for the National Goods Year

— Ai Wu

1. Raise the Level of Consumption: Promoting national goods truly requires promoting manufacturing and increasing production. More importantly, it requires raising the level of consumption of national goods among our people. Once the level of consumption rises, national goods will sell well. Seeing the potential for profit, everyone will be willing to manufacture national goods. If the level of consumption does not rise, merely promoting manufacturing will result in stockpiled goods, financial stagnation, factory bankruptcies, worker unemployment, and overproduction, which is very dangerous. There are many ways to raise the level of consumption, including promotion, publicity, and rewards. I believe the most effective method is for all public and private organizations nationwide to unite and require all employees, large and small, to wear and use national goods. Within a year, this will surely shift the atmosphere. As the ancients said, "The virtue of a ruler is like the wind; the virtue of the people is like grass. When the wind blows upon the grass, it must bend." There are many such examples throughout history that are readily available.

2. Pay Attention to the Price of Goods: Affordable and high-quality products are the key to promoting national goods. If the price is low but the quality is not good, only a small number of people in the lower middle class will buy them. If the quality is good but the price is not affordable, only a small number of people in the upper class will buy them. If the quality is not good and the price is not affordable, then no one will ask about them, which is only logical. A common problem among Chinese people is that once a product sells well, they either cut corners on materials or raise the price, which is equivalent to suicide. This is something everyone should pay serious attention to in the future.

3. Protect Invention Rights: Inventing something takes a lot of effort. When others see that it is profitable, they all start to imitate it, leading to oversupply and forcing prices down to sell off inventory. You lower the price, and I lower the price. The price keeps dropping until it becomes unprofitable. The result is a lose-lose situation, creating opportunities for foreign goods to invade. Therefore, in the future, anyone who makes an invention should register it with the legal authorities. Once registered, their invention rights should be effectively protected. With this approach, everyone will naturally put in hard work and not dare to take shortcuts.

4. Train National Goods Personnel: It is certainly necessary to train manufacturing personnel, but it is also necessary to train sales personnel. To ensure that the training is effective, experts should be hired to handle it. This is fundamental to promoting national goods, and petty expenses should not be spared. Just taking the training of sales personnel as an example, how to train their skills? How to supplement their knowledge? How to cultivate their morals? These are all very complex issues.

The national goods industry in the National Goods Year should earnestly carry out these four tasks. Without uttering empty slogans, without being greedy for more than one can handle, and without working sporadically, I can confidently say that the future of national goods will definitely be bright.

National Goods News

Minutes of the Founding Meeting of China National Goods Co., Ltd.

Time: 3:00 PM, January 20, 1933

Location: Shanghai Bankers Association, No. 4 Hong Kong Road, Shanghai. Section Chief Wu Huanru, representative of the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau, attended to provide guidance. (1) 225 shareholders and representatives attended, holding a total of 3,956 shares, all exceeding the legal quorum. The meeting was declared open. (2) Mr. Pan Yangyao was publicly elected as chairman. (3) The chairman led the attendees in customary rituals. (4) The chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting, stating that after several months of preparation, the company had now fully collected its share capital and the number of attendees and shares met the legal requirements. Therefore, the founding meeting was naturally established. (5) Section Chief Wu Huanru, representative of the Social Bureau, delivered a speech, expressing his great pleasure in participating in the founding meeting of China National Goods Co., Ltd., as national goods companies were still a pioneering endeavor in China. In recent years, while serving in the Social Bureau, supervising agriculture, industry, and commerce, he had deeply felt the importance of promoting national goods and had several times considered using temple properties and public land to build a large-scale national goods market, but all efforts had been unsuccessful due to various difficulties. This shows that although the government has great determination to promote national goods, it still requires the efforts of the business community to have an effect. This company is organized by a union of major national goods factories, and the managers of each factory are successful entrepreneurs. Now, the minds, talents, and experiences of so many successful people are combined to run a large-scale national goods company, and its future is bright, which can be confidently asserted. (6) Chief Preparer Mr. Fang Yexian reported on the preparatory process, stating that the company was initiated around September of last year. At that time, the Nine Factories National Goods Temporary Market, formed by nine factories including China Chemical Industrial Society and China Enamel Factory, had achieved satisfactory results, so there was a motion to organize a permanent national goods market. However, most national goods markets in Shanghai were disorganized and unsystematic, making management extremely difficult. Therefore, it was decided to adopt a company structure. A preparatory office was established on November 1st of last year to begin preparations. A business location was rented at the Mainland Market, and equipment was prepared and the building was decorated, all of which has now been completed. The share capital of 100,000 yuan has also been fully collected. The interest on the share capital amounted to 61.13 yuan. This share capital and interest have been deposited in the Hongkou branch of the Bank of China and Xinhua Bank, respectively. As for the funds for acquiring assets and decorations, not all have been paid yet. The establishment cost is 3,201.94 yuan. (7) Discussion of proposals: A. Discussion of the company's articles of association. Resolution: The draft was approved with amendments, with no dissent. (8) Election of directors and supervisors: A. Elected directors: Fang Yexian (2,997 votes), Cai Shengbai (2,789 votes), Ren Shigang (2,788 votes), Wang Zhixin (2,746 votes), Fang Jiangge (2,691 votes), Ye Youcai (2,480 votes), Pan Yangyao (2,382 votes), Shi Liangcai (2,000 votes), Zhang Huikang (1,943 votes). Next highest votes: Xu Yangnan (987 votes), Xiang Kangyuan (559 votes), Huang Shoumin (508 votes), Wang Boyuan (484 votes), Mu Ouchu (424 votes). B. Elected supervisors: Cheng Nianpeng (1,768 votes), Huang Yanfang (1,557 votes). Next highest votes: Xu Guanqun (438 votes), Xiang Kangyuan (347 votes), Wang Zhenfang (251 votes). (9) Investigation report by the elected directors and supervisors: A. All 5,000 shares have been fully subscribed. B. The payable share capital of 100,000 yuan has been paid in full at one time. C. None of the shareholders used property other than cash to pay for their shares. D. The establishment expenses borne by the company are legitimate. E. The initiators did not receive any special remuneration.

Country Bumpkin

— Shen Youshi

I am just a commoner; how am I qualified to say nonsensical things in this large Shen Bao National Goods Weekly? However, I see many celebrities publishing very valuable articles in the National Goods Weekly, which unconsciously makes me envious and I want to say a few words to relieve my boredom. Fortunately, "The rise and fall of the nation is the responsibility of every individual." I will speak from the perspective of a commoner.

I am a country person, someone who eats chalk dust, a primary school teacher despised by everyone. When I go to the city, especially Shanghai, everyone unanimously says, "Country bumpkin." Because my clothes are entirely made of homespun cloth, I am bestowed with this elegant nickname. Mr. Yinge says, "This is the psychology of national subjugation." But in the countryside, who dares to call me a country bumpkin? Therefore, the countryside does not have this psychology of national subjugation. So, the nation is being subjugated in the cities, not in the countryside!

What truly surprises me is that when Mr. Wu Zhihui wears homespun clothes, people praise him for promoting national goods. However, when I wear them, it has the opposite effect!

I understand! They are important figures, and we are insignificant fleas. Insignificant fleas are not worthy of saving the nation; important figures are the ones who should save the nation!

That's not right! I am clearly promoting national goods; I am saving the nation, but people scold me, and those who scold me are so-called enlightened city people. Alas! The nation is being ruined by you city people, especially those important figures! Otherwise, why would Mr. Wu be praised so profusely for promoting national goods? Country people promote national goods every day, but who says they are patriotic?

Also, the editor of the National Goods Weekly says, "The bride and groom must use national goods before I will be their wedding witness..." What is so strange about that! Look at the country people; people get married every day wearing homespun cloth. Who praises them? It is clear that city people use foreign goods, especially the important figures. If someone happens to wear homespun cloth, they are greatly surprised! I cannot help but sigh again, "China is being ruined by those people!"

From this, it can be seen that the more knowledgeable people are, the more they sing about promoting national goods. I hope – and this is a harsh saying – that each of them can refrain from using foreign goods themselves!

These words may offend many city people, and the editor will probably just smile coldly and throw them in the wastepaper basket. But the facts are so clear and obvious, and because a commoner also has the responsibility to save the nation, I have written them out after class despite the laborious effort. If anyone sympathizes with me, that is my only hope! I hope anyone with brilliant ideas will offer their advice!
